## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This task models the acceleration of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator. The acceleration dv/dt depends on position x (restoring force, possibly nonlinear), velocity v (damping/self-excitation), and potentially time t (external driving). Classical nonlinear oscillator models like Duffing, van der Pol, and driven oscillators provide the relevant formula structures.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear restoring force: dv_dt = c0 * x (simple harmonic oscillator)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Duffing with quintic: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order nonlinear restoring)
- Damped linear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear damping plus restoring force)
- Damped Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (Duffing with linear damping)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * x**2 * v (nonlinear damping with position-dependent coefficient)
- Driven oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (externally driven with sinusoidal force)
- Driven Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (driven nonlinear oscillator)
- Cubic damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (nonlinear velocity-dependent friction)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (Rayleigh-type nonlinear damping)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * cos(c1 * t) (time-varying stiffness / Mathieu equation)
- Softening/hardening spring with damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * x**2 * v (combined nonlinear restoring and damping)
- General polynomial restoring: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 (asymmetric nonlinear potential)
- Coulomb-like friction: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * (c2 + c3 * x**2) (generalized van der Pol form)
- Velocity-position coupling: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x * v + c2 * x * v**2 (mixed nonlinear coupling terms)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x³, x⁵) → symmetric potential wells preserving oscillatory behavior
- Even-power position terms (x²) in restoring force → asymmetric potential, indicating broken symmetry
- Product terms x²·v or (1-x²)·v → amplitude-dependent damping characteristic of self-sustained oscillations (van der Pol type)
- Sinusoidal time dependence sin(c·t) or cos(c·t) → external periodic driving force or parametric excitation
- Cubic velocity terms v³ → nonlinear drag that dominates at high speeds (Rayleigh dissipation)
- Position-velocity product x·v → energy-dependent coupling, often arising from coordinate transformations
- Absence of explicit time dependence → autonomous system; presence suggests forced/parametric oscillator
- Sign of the coefficient of x determines stability: negative coefficient (restoring) vs positive (repulsive)

GT Equivalence Verification (PO38)
============================================================
GT: -beta*sin(v) - mu*(c0 - x**c1)*v - omega0**c2*x*exp(-Abs(x))
Candidate formulas: 50

I need to determine if any candidate formula can match the GT:

**GT:** `-0.1948*v*(1 - x²) - 3.0492*x*exp(-|x|) - 0.1430*sin(v)`

The GT has three main components:
1. **`-μ*(1-x²)*v`** = `-0.1948*v + 0.1948*v*x²` (linear in v, and v*x² term)
2. **`-ω₀²*x*exp(-|x|)`** = `-3.0492*x*exp(-|x|)` (x times exponential of -|x|)
3. **`-β*sin(v)`** = `-0.1430*sin(v)` (sine of v, NOT x)

**Key challenges:**
- The term `exp(-|x|)` involves absolute value, which is **not** equivalent to `exp(c*x²)` or any smooth function of x.
- The `sin(v)` term is a nonlinear function of v.

Let me check candidates systematically:

**The sin(v) term:** Most candidates don't have a sin(v) term. They approximate it with polynomial terms like `v³` (since sin(v) ≈ v - v³/6 + ...). This is only an approximation, not exact equivalence.

**The exp(-|x|) term:** Candidates use `exp(c*x²)` which is a smooth, even function of x. But `exp(-|x|)` is not smooth at x=0 and behaves differently. `exp(-|x|)` cannot equal `exp(c*x²)` for any constant c.

Let me check if any candidate has both `sin(v)` (or equivalent via phase shift) AND `exp(-|x|)`:

None of the candidates contain `sin(v)`, `cos(v)`, or `exp(-|x|)` or `exp(-Abs(x))`.

**Can we approximate?** No - the question asks for mathematical equivalence, not approximation.

**Checking candidates with `v*exp(c*x²)` terms (3, 10, 36, 40, 44, 45, 46):** These have `v*exp(c*x²)` which could potentially represent `v*(1-x²)` if the exponential could match, but `exp(c*x²)` ≠ polynomial. Also, none handle `sin(v)` or `exp(-|x|)`.

**Candidates with log terms (22, 47):** `log(c*exp(c*x²)+1)` — this doesn't help match `exp(-|x|)` or `sin(v)`.

**Candidates with time-dependent terms (24-31, 34, 49):** The GT has no explicit time dependence, so any `sin(c*t)` or `cos(c*t)` terms would need coefficients of 0, reducing these to simpler forms that still can't match.

**Critical analysis:** 
- No candidate contains `sin(v)` or `cos(v)`, so sin(v) cannot be exactly represented.
- No candidate contains `exp(-|x|)` or `exp(-Abs(x))`, so the `x*exp(-|x|)` term cannot be represented.
- `exp(c*x²)` with c<0 gives a Gaussian, which is smooth and symmetric, unlike `exp(-|x|)` which has a cusp at 0.

Even if we tried to use `x*exp(c*x²)` to match `x*exp(-|x|)`, these are fundamentally different functions (one is Gaussian-like, the other is Laplacian-like). They cannot be made equal for all x.

Similarly, polynomial approximations of `sin(v)` (like `c*v + c*v³ + c*v⁵`) cannot exactly equal `sin(v)` for all v.

Since mathematical equivalence requires the expressions to be identical for all values of the variables (x, v, t), and no candidate has the functional forms needed to exactly represent either `sin(v)` or `x*exp(-|x|)`, none of the candidates can match the GT.

GT Equivalence Verification (PO38)

GT: -beta*sin(v) - mu*(c0 - x**c1)*v - omega0**c2*x*exp(-Abs(x))
Candidates evaluated: 50
Matched candidate IDs: []

I need to determine which candidates can exactly match the Ground Truth:

**GT:** `-0.194830767863936*v*(1 - x²) - 3.04923978373096*x*exp(-|x|) - 0.143047751034959*sin(v)`

Let me analyze the GT's structure:
1. **v-terms:** `-0.1948*v + 0.1948*v*x²` (linear in v, with x² coupling)
2. **x-exponential term:** `-3.049*x*exp(-|x|)` — note the **absolute value** of x
3. **sin(v) term:** `-0.1430*sin(v)`

The key challenge is matching `x*exp(-|x|)` and `sin(v)`.

**For `sin(v)`:** Its Taylor series is `v - v³/6 + v⁵/120 - ...`. So candidates need either `sin(v)` explicitly or terms like `v + v³ + v⁵ + ...` to approximate it. But approximation ≠ exact match. Candidates with `v + v³` terms could potentially absorb the `sin(v)` only if they have ALL odd powers of v (which none do). So candidates using polynomial `v` terms to replace `sin(v)` are NOT exact matches.

**For `x*exp(-|x|)`:** Note `|x|` makes this non-analytic at x=0. `exp(-|x|)` is NOT equal to `exp(-x²)` or any polynomial in x. Also `exp(-|x|)` ≠ `exp(c*x²)` for any c. The function `x*exp(-|x|)` is an even-in-absolute-value function that can't be represented by `x*exp(c*x²)`.

Wait — let me reconsider. `x*exp(-|x|)` is odd in x (since |−x| = |x|, so (−x)*exp(−|−x|) = −x*exp(−|x|)). Meanwhile `x*exp(c*x²)` is also odd. But `exp(-|x|)` has a cusp at x=0 while `exp(c*x²)` is smooth. These are fundamentally different functions and cannot be equal for all x.

Similarly, `1/(c1 + x²)` is smooth and cannot replicate `exp(-|x|)`.

No finite combination of polynomials, `x*exp(c*x²)`, `x/(c+x²)`, etc. can exactly equal `x*exp(-|x|)` due to the non-analytic nature of `|x|`.

And no finite polynomial in v can exactly equal `sin(v)`.

Let me check if ANY candidate has both `exp(-|x|)` and `sin(v)` — scanning all candidates... None contain `|x|` or `Abs(x)` or `sin(v)`.

Therefore, **no candidate can exactly match the GT**. Every candidate either:
- Lacks `sin(v)` (trying to approximate with `v + v³` polynomials), or
- Lacks `exp(-|x|)` (using `exp(c*x²)` or polynomials instead)

Both substitutions are approximations, not exact equivalences.

Candidate 1-50 verdict analysis: All candidates use either polynomial terms in v (like v, v³, v⁵) or smooth exponentials (exp(c*x²), exp(c*v²)) or rational functions. None can exactly reproduce `sin(v)` or `x*exp(-|x|)`.
